## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and current concentration, which is the core problem of chemical reaction kinetics — determining the rate law governing a reaction.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate coefficient)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill equation type)
- Parallel pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple reaction pathways)
- Exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (concentration-dependent activation energy analog)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is strictly proportional to a power of A with no explicit time dependence, the system follows a simple autonomous rate law — use power-law forms A**n
- If the rate changes sign at a specific concentration value, this suggests a reversible reaction approaching equilibrium — look for (A - c) terms or (c - A) factors
- If the rate saturates at high concentration, enzyme-like or surface-adsorption mechanisms are involved — use rational functions A/(c + A)
- If the rate has a maximum at intermediate concentration, substrate inhibition or autocatalytic behavior is present — use A*(c - A) or A/(c + A**2) forms
- If residuals show systematic time dependence after fitting A-only models, the rate constant itself may be time-varying — introduce multiplicative time-dependent factors
- Negative values of dA_dt indicate consumption (reactant), positive values indicate production (product) — the sign of leading coefficients encodes reaction directionality
- If log(|dA_dt|) vs log(A) is linear, the reaction follows simple power-law kinetics and the slope gives the reaction order
- Competition between formation and degradation pathways often manifests as a sum of terms with opposite signs: c0*A**n - c1*A**m

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) + c1*_w*cos(log(A + c2))
Candidate formulas: 60

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `-0.2597*sqrt(A) + 0.9123*cos(log(A + 1))`.

The GT has two terms:
1. A term proportional to `sqrt(A)` (i.e., `A^(1/2)`)
2. A `cos(log(A + 1))` term

Let me scan for candidates that could produce both `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))` terms.

**Candidate 3**: `A*c0/(A + c1)**2 + c2*log(c3*exp(A*c4) + 1) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)`

The third term: `c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)`. If c7=1, c6=1, c8=π/2, this becomes `c5*cos(log(A+1))`. That matches the cosine term! But the first two terms need to produce `-0.2597*sqrt(A)`. The first term is `A*c0/(A+c1)^2` which is a rational function, and the second is `c2*log(c3*exp(A*c4)+1)` which for c4→0 approaches a constant. Neither can produce `sqrt(A)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 14**: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3/(A**c2 + c4) + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8 + 1) + c9)`

The sin term with c9=π/2 becomes `c6*cos(c7*log(A*c8+1))`. Set c7=1, c8=1: `c6*cos(log(A+1))`. ✓
Now need remaining terms to give `-0.2597*sqrt(A)`. Set c0=0, c1=0, c5=0. Then: `A^c2 * c3/(A^c2 + c4)`. Set c2=1/2: `sqrt(A)*c3/(sqrt(A)+c4)`. This is NOT `sqrt(A)` — it's a different function. **No match.**

**Candidate 24**: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3/(A**c2 + c4) + c5 + c6*cos(c7*log(A**c8*c9 + 1))`

Set c0=0, c1=0, c5=0. The cos term: set c8=1, c9=1, c7=1: `c6*cos(log(A+1))`. ✓
Remaining: `A^c2 * c3/(A^c2 + c4)`. Same issue as above — can't be `sqrt(A)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 43**: `A**3*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6)`

Set c0=0, c1=0, c2=0. Sin term with c6=π/2: `c3*cos(c4*log(A*c5+1))`. Set c4=1, c5=1. This gives `c3*cos(log(A+1))`. But remaining terms are polynomials in A — can't give `sqrt(A)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 58**: `A^(5/2)*c0/(sqrt(A)*c1+1) + A^(3/2)*c2/(sqrt(A)*c1+1) + sqrt(A)*c3/(sqrt(A)*c1+1) + A^2*c4/(sqrt(A)*c1+1) + A*c5/(sqrt(A)*c1+1) + c6/(sqrt(A)*c1+1) + c7/(sqrt(A)*c1+1)`

Set c1=0: denominator=1. Then terms are `c0*A^(5/2) + c2*A^(3/2) + c3*sqrt(A) + c4*A^2 + c5*A + (c6+c7)`. This can produce `sqrt(A)` but has no cosine term. **No match.**

**Candidate 25**: `A*c0/(A+c1)**2 + c2*log(c3*exp(A*c4)+1) + c5*sin(A*c6 + c7 + c8*log(A*c9+1))`

The sin argument: `A*c6 + c7 + c8*log(A*c9+1)`. Set c6=0, c9=1, c8=1, c7=π/2: `sin(π/2 + log(A+1)) = cos(log(A+1))`. ✓
Remaining: set c0=0, c4→0 so log term → constant. But need `sqrt(A)` from somewhere. Can't get it. **No match.**

After checking all candidates, none can produce both `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))` simultaneously.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK9)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) + c1*_w*cos(log(A + c2))
Candidates evaluated: 60
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: `-0.2597*sqrt(A) + 0.9123*cos(log(A + 1))`**

This has two basis functions: `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))`.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. The key question for each is: can it produce exactly `c*sqrt(A) + d*cos(log(A+1))` for some constant choices?

**Key observations about GT:**
- It contains `sqrt(A)` - a fractional power
- It contains `cos(log(A+1))` - a cosine of a logarithm
- No polynomial terms, no exponential terms, no `t` dependence
- The function `cos(log(A+1))` is oscillatory in `log(A+1)`

Let me go through candidates, focusing on whether they can produce these specific basis functions.

**Candidates with `sin` or `cos` of `log(...)` terms** (most promising):

**Candidate 3:** `A*c0/(A+c1)^2 + c2*log(c3*exp(A*c4)+1) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1)+c8)`
- The third term: `c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1)+c8)` with c6=1, c7=1, c8=π/2 gives `c5*cos(log(A+1))` ✓
- First term: `A*c0/(A+c1)^2` - can this equal `k*sqrt(A)`? No, this is a rational function, not a fractional power.
- Second term: `c2*log(c3*exp(A*c4)+1)` - set c4=0, this becomes `c2*log(c3+1)` = constant. Or set c2=0.
- If c0=0 and c2=0, we get only `c5*cos(log(A+1))`, missing `sqrt(A)`.
- We need `sqrt(A)` from somewhere. The rational function `A/(A+c1)^2` cannot equal `sqrt(A)`. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 14:** `A^2*c0 + A*c1 + A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4) + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8+1)+c9)`
- Last term with c7=1, c8=1, c9=π/2: `c6*cos(log(A+1))` ✓
- `A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4)`: set c2=1/2, then `sqrt(A)*c3/(sqrt(A)+c4)`. This is NOT `sqrt(A)`.
- Set c0=c1=0, c5=0. We need `A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4) = k*sqrt(A)`.
  With c2=1/2: `c3*sqrt(A)/(sqrt(A)+c4)`. Setting c4=0: `c3*sqrt(A)/sqrt(A) = c3` = constant. Not sqrt(A).
  We can't get `sqrt(A)` from this term. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 24:** `A^2*c0 + A*c1 + A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4) + c5 + c6*cos(c7*log(A^c8*c9+1))`
- Last term: `c6*cos(c7*log(c9*A^c8+1))`. Set c8=1, c9=1, c7=1: `c6*cos(log(A+1))` ✓
- Need `sqrt(A)` from remaining: `A^2*c0 + A*c1 + A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4) + c5`
- Set c0=c1=0, c5=0. `A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4)` with c2=1/2: `c3*sqrt(A)/(sqrt(A)+c4)`. Set c4=0: constant. Not sqrt(A).
- What if c4→0 but keeping the ratio? `c3*sqrt(A)/(sqrt(A)+c4)` ≠ `k*sqrt(A)` for all A. **[NO MATCH]**

Wait, let me reconsider. What about c2=1/2 and expanding? `c3*A^(1/2)/(A^(1/2)+c4)` - this approaches c3 for large A and c3*sqrt(A)/c4 for small A. It's never exactly sqrt(A).

**Candidate 43:** `A^3*c0 + A^2*c1 + A*c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5+1)+c6)`
- Set c0=c1=c2=0: `c3*sin(c4*log(c5*A+1)+c6)` = `c3*cos(log(A+1))` with c4=1,c5=1,c6=π/2.
- But we lose `sqrt(A)`. Polynomials can't produce `sqrt(A)`. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 44:** `A*c0 + A*c1/(c2*t+c3) + c4 + c5/(c2*t+c3) + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8+1)+c9)`
- Set c1=c5=0 to remove t: `A*c0 + c4 + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8+1)+c9)`. Missing sqrt(A). **[NO MATCH]**

Let me check all remaining candidates systematically for the ability to produce both `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))`.

Most candidates use combinations of: polynomials, rational functions, exponentials, logarithms, and occasionally sin/cos. The GT requires `sqrt(A)` AND `cos(log(A+1))`. Very few candidates have both a fractional power mechanism AND a trig-of-log mechanism.

**Candidate 25:** `A*c0/(A+c1)^2 + c2*log(c3*exp(A*c4)+1) + c5*sin(A*c6+c7+c8*log(A*c9+1))`
- Third term: `c5*sin(c8*log(A*c9+1) + A*c6 + c7)`. Set c6=0, c8=1, c9=1, c7=π/2: `c5*cos(log(A+1))` ✓
- Still need sqrt(A) from first two terms. Can't get it. **[NO MATCH]**

After exhaustive analysis, none of the candidates can produce both `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))` simultaneously.

Let me verify all candidates one final time... None have an explicit `sqrt(A)` or `A^(1/2)` term except **Candidate 18** and **Candidate 58**.

**Candidate 18:** `sqrt(A)*c0 + A*c1/(A+c2)^2 + c3*log(c4*exp(A*c5)+1) + c6/A`
- `sqrt(A)*c0` ✓ for sqrt(A)
- But no cos(log(...)) term. Has log and rational functions only. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 58:** Rational in sqrt(A) - polynomial in sqrt(A). No trig. **[NO MATCH]**

None of the candidates can produce both required basis functions.
